        4.  Abhi 'Logo' aur 'Button' dono left mein chipke honge (kyunki Spacing Mode 'Packed' hai).
        5.  "Navbar" Frame ko select rakhein. Right Panel (Auto Layout section) mein `Spacing between items` (e.g., 16px) ke paas `...` (Advanced) par click karein.
        6.  `Spacing mode` ko `Packed` se `Space between (Auto)` kar dein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Magic! 'Logo' apne aap 'Navbar' ke left end par chala jayega aur 'Button' apne aap right end par chala jayega. Ab aap 'Navbar' ki width ko (mouse se) stretch karke dekhein, woh hamesha ends par chipke rahenge.
    * **Task 2 (Fill Container):**
        1.  Ek Vertical Auto Layout Frame ("Card") banayein.
        2.  Uske andar ek Text ('Title') aur doosra Text ('Paragraph') rakhein.
        3.  'Title' Text ki width `Hug Contents` rakhein.
        4.  'Paragraph' Text ki width `Fill Container` set karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Ab jab aap "Card" Frame ko chauda (wide) karenge, toh 'Title' utna hi rahega, lekin 'Paragraph' text apne aap stretch hokar poori card ki width le lega aur text wrap ho jayega.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * `Fill Container` aur `Hug Contents` ka fark na samajhna.
    * `Space between` property ko na dhoondh paana (yeh 'Spacing' field mein 'Auto' type karke bhi aa jaati hai).
    * *Child* (element) ki jagah *Parent* (container) par Resizing property dhoondhna. (Resizing hamesha child par lagti hai, ki woh parent ke hisaab se kaise behave kare).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Itna complex kyun hai? Main bas haath se desktop aur mobile ke 2 alag-alag design nahi bana sakta?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Aap bana sakte hain, par usmein time double lagega. Ek student 'Fill Container' ka use karke *ek hi* design banata hai. Woh mobile frame (375px) ko resize karke desktop (1440px) banata hai, aur 'Fill Container' waale elements (jaise text blocks, background cards) apne aap stretch ho jaate hain.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Team mein 'base component' (e.g., ek Card) Auto Layout aur Resizing rules ke saath banaya jaata hai. Phir designer us component ko mobile, tablet, desktop... *kahin bhi* daalta hai, aur component apne aap us jagah (container) mein fit ho jaata hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Twitter/X ka poora layout. Left sidebar (Fixed Width), Center Timeline (Fill Container), Right Sidebar (Fixed Width). Yeh poora ek bada Horizontal Auto Layout hai. Jab aap browser window choti-badi karte hain, toh sirf Center Timeline (Fill) chota-bada hota hai, sidebars fixed rehte hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * **Hug Contents:** Buttons, Tags, Pills (jahan size text par depend kare).
    * **Fill Container:** Text blocks, Backgrounds, Inputs (jahan size parent par depend kare).
    * **Space between:** Navbars, List items (jahan ek cheez left aur ek right chahiye).
    * Hamesha *child* element ko select karke uski 'Resizing' property set karein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **`Space between` kaam nahi kar raha!** Check karein ki aapke Auto Layout Frame ki width 'Fixed' ya 'Fill Container' hai. Agar parent ki width 'Hug' hogi, toh 'Space between' ke liye jagah hi nahi bachegi.
    * **Absolute Position kya hai?** Yeh ek 'escape hatch' (bhagne ka raasta) hai. Agar aapko Auto Layout Frame ke *andar* ek element (jaise Notification dot) ko manually (haath se) position karna ho (e.g., top-right corner par), toh us element ko select karke 'Absolute Position' (Right panel, Frame section mein) on kar dein.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Navbar' waali exercise (Task 1) ko dobara karein.
    * 2. Ek 'Profile Card' (Vertical Auto Layout) banayein. Uske andar Image (Fixed), Name (Hug), aur Bio (Fill Container) rakhein. Card ko stretch karke dekhein ki Bio text kaise react karta hai.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * (Auto Layout hi sab kuch hai. Iski practice hi sabse zaroori hai).

---

### 4.6: Constraints

**(Yeh ek CORE Foundational topic hai. Poora dhyaan dein.)**

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Constraints ğŸ“Œ (Elements ko Frame se 'pin' karna).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Constraints rules ka ek set hai jo aap **non-Auto Layout Frame** ke andar elements par lagate hain. Yeh batata hai ki jab parent 'Frame' (screen) ka size badlega, toh andar ka element (e.g., button) Frame ke kis hisse (left, right, top, bottom, center) se chipka (pinned) rahega.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh "Responsive Design" ka *doosra* tareeka hai. Auto Layout (naya aur behtar) aane se pele, Constraints hi ekmaatr tareeka tha. Yeh abhi bhi *bohot* zaroori hai **jab aap Auto Layout use *nahi* kar rahe hon** (e.g., ek complex layout jahan cheezein overlap ho rahi hon, ya floating buttons).
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab aapke paas ek 'Normal Frame' (Auto Layout *nahi*) ho aur aap use responsive banana chahte hon. **Sabse common use:** Ek "Floating Action Button" (FAB) banana, jo screen ke 'Bottom-Right' mein hamesha chipka rehta hai, chahe screen choti ho ya badi. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh 'manual resizing' ki problem solve karta hai (jab Auto Layout use na ho raha ho).
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Agar aapne ek normal Frame (e.g., iPhone 14) ko resize karke (e.g., Desktop) bada kiya, toh saare elements (jo default 'Top' aur 'Left' par constrained hote hain) *left-top corner* mein hi ikatthe ho jayenge. Aapka design poori tarah toot jayega.
6.  **ğŸ§‘_ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown (Right Panel 'Constraints'):**_
    * Yeh section aapko tab dikhta hai jab aap ek element ko *normal Frame* ke andar select karte hain.
    * Ek box dikhta hai jismein blue dotted lines hoti hain.
    * **Horizontal (X-axis):** Left (Default), Right, Left & Right, Center, Scale.
    * **Vertical (Y-axis):** Top (Default), Bottom, Top & Bottom, Center, Scale.
    * **Example:** Ek element ko 'Right' aur 'Bottom' par set karne ka matlab hai: "Jab parent Frame resize ho, toh is element ki doori *right* edge se aur *bottom* edge se same (fixed) rakhna."
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek 'Floating Button' banana jo hamesha bottom-right mein rahe.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  `F` daba kar ek 'iPhone 14' Frame banayein. (Yeh normal Frame hai, Auto Layout *nahi* hai).
        2.  `O` daba kar ek Circle (button) banayein aur use Frame ke *bottom-right corner* mein rakhein.
        3.  Button (Circle) ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'Constraints' section dekhein.
        4.  Default Constraint `Left` aur `Top` par set hoga.
        5.  Horizontal (blue line) ko `Left` se badal kar `Right` par click karein.
        6.  Vertical (blue line) ko `Top` se badal kar `Bottom` par click karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Ab iPhone 14 Frame ko select karein aur uska size mouse se kheench kar bada ya chota karein. Button hamesha bottom-right corner se *chipka* (pinned) rahega.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * **Auto Layout Frame ke andar Constraints dhoondhna.** (Nahi milenge! Auto Layout (Topic 4.4) aur Constraints (Topic 4.6) do *alag* system hain. Ek Frame ya toh Auto Layout ho sakta hai, ya Constraints, dono ek saath nahi).
    * Default (Left & Top) Constraints ko na badalna.
    * 'Scale' (jo element ko stretch karta hai) aur 'Center' (jo element ko beech mein rakhta hai) mein confuse hona.
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main Auto Layout (4.4) seekh raha hoon. Kya mujhe Constraints (4.6) ki bhi zaroorat hai? Yeh confusing hai."
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Haan, 100% zaroorat hai. Auto Layout aapke 90% kaam (Buttons, Lists, Cards) ke liye hai. Lekin us 10% kaam ke liye jahan elements *overlap* karte hain (e.g., ek background image ke upar text), wahan aapko Normal Frame + Constraints ki zaroorat padegi.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** **Pro Rule:** Pehli pasand hamesha 'Auto Layout' hai. Agar koi layout Auto Layout se *nahi* ban paa raha hai (e.g., ek map par pins lagana, ya complex overlapping collage), *tab hi* Normal Frame + Constraints ka istemaal kiya jaata hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Ek website ka 'Header'. Header ek Normal Frame hai (Auto Layout nahi hai). Andar 'Logo' (Constraint: Left, Center Vertical), 'Nav Links' (Constraint: Center, Center Vertical), aur 'Login Button' (Constraint: Right, Center Vertical) rakhe hain. Jab Frame (screen) stretch hota hai, sab apni jagah rehte hain. (Note: Yahi kaam Auto Layout ke 'Space between' se bhi ho sakta hai).
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * **Rule 1: Auto Layout > Constraints.** Pehle Auto Layout try karo.
    * **Rule 2:** Agar Auto Layout se kaam na chale (e.g., overlapping), tabhi Normal Frame + Constraints use karo.
    * Constraints lagane ke baad, hamesha parent Frame ko resize karke test karo ki woh sahi behave kar raha hai ya nahi.
    * **Left & Right (Scale):** Element horizontal stretch hoga.
    * **Top & Bottom (Scale):** Element vertical stretch hoga.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Auto Layout Frame ke andar 'Constraints' kahan gaye?** Wahan 'Constraints' ko 'Resizing' (Hug, Fill, Fixed) kehte hain (Topic 4.5). 'Fill Container' (Auto Layout) = 'Left & Right' (Constraints). Dono ka concept same hai, naam alag hain.
    * **Kya main Auto Layout aur Constraints mix kar sakta hoon?** Haan. Aap ek Normal Frame (jispar Constraints kaam karte hain) ke andar ek Auto Layout Frame (jo khud responsive hai) *nest* kar sakte hain.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Floating Button' waali exercise (Task) ko dobara karein.
    * 2. Ek Desktop Frame banayein. Uske andar ek Rectangle (Header) banayein. Us Rectangle ko Constraints (Left & Right, Top) dein. Ab Frame ki width change karke dekhein, Header stretch hona chahiye.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * (Yeh Figma ka core feature hai. Practice hi key hai).

---

### 4.7: Scale Tool & Viewport Resizing

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Scale Tool (K) & Viewport Resizing (Design ko chota-bada karna).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):**
    * **Scale Tool (K):** Yeh ek special tool (Toolbar mein Move (V) ke neeche) hai jo aapke *poore* design (font size, stroke, padding, sab kuch) ko proportionately (anupaatik roop se) chota ya bada karta hai.
    * **Viewport Resizing:** Yeh 'Prototype' tab mein ek option hai jo batata hai ki aapka prototype (clickable design) alag-alag screen sizes par *display* (dikhega) kaise.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** 'Scale Tool' tab zaroori hai jab aapne design galat size mein bana diya (e.g., Desktop design 2000px mein bana diya, aur ab 1440px mein chahiye). 'Viewport Resizing' zaroori hai prototype ko real-world mein test karne ke liye.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):**
    * **Scale Tool (K):** Jab aapko ek *poora* Frame (aur uske andar ki har cheez) 2x bada ya 0.5x chota karna ho. Jaise ek Desktop design ko copy karke Mobile design *jaisa* banana (scaling down).
    * **Viewport Resizing:** Jab aap prototype 'Present' (Play button) karte hain.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):**
    * **Scale Tool (K) ke bina:** Agar aap Frame ko 'Move Tool' (V) se bada karenge, toh sirf Frame bada hoga, andar ka content (font size, button size) utna hi rahega (jab tak Constraints/Auto Layout na lage hon). 'Scale' tool *sab kuch* bada karta hai (font 16px se 32px ho jayega).
    * **Viewport Resizing ke bina:** Aapka prototype hamesha 100% (original size) par dikhega, jo shayad aapki browser window mein fit na ho.
6.  **ğŸ§‘_ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**_
    * **Scale Tool (K):**
        1.  Toolbar se `K` (Scale Tool) chunein.
        2.  Frame ko select karein.
        3.  Corner se drag karke chota/bada karein.
        4.  *Sab kuch* (font, stroke, padding) scale ho jayega.
    * **Viewport Resizing (Prototype Tab):**
        1.  `Prototype` tab (Right Panel) par jaayein.
        2.  'Device' (e.g., iPhone 14) chunein.
        3.  Neeche 'Viewport' section mein 3 options hote hain:
            * `100% - Display at actual size:` Prototype 100% size par dikhega (badi screens ke liye).
            * `Fit to Screen:` Prototype chota hokar aapki display window mein fit ho jayega (Mobile app ko desktop par dekhne ke liye best).
            * `Fill Screen:` Prototype stretch/zoom hokar poori window bhar dega.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek Desktop design (1440px) ko scale down karke Tablet size (e.g., 768px) banana.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation (Scale Tool):**
        1.  Apna 1440px waala 'Desktop' Frame select karein.
        2.  `K` dabayein (Scale Tool).
        3.  Right Panel (Scale section) mein, '1x' (default) ki jagah `0.53x` type karein (768/1440 = 0.53). Ya corner se drag karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapke paas ek naya, chota Frame hoga (768px). *Lekin* uske andar font size (e.g., 64px se 34px) aur padding (e.g., 24px se 13px) bhi ajeeb numbers mein scale ho gaye honge.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * **'Scale Tool' (K) ko responsive design ka tareeka samajhna.** (Sabse badi galti!). 'Scale' tool cheezon ko proportionately chota karta hai, 'responsive' nahi banata. Responsive design (Mobile/Desktop) 'Auto Layout' aur 'Constraints' se *manually* banaya jaata hai. 'Scale' sirf ek 'dumb' tool hai.
    * 'Move Tool' (V) aur 'Scale Tool' (K) ke fark ko na samajhna.
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Toh main 'Scale' tool se Desktop design ko chota karke Mobile design bana sakta hoon na?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** **Nahi!** Aisa mat karna. Scale karne se aapke font size 13.5px, padding 7.8px ho jayegi, jo 8-point grid ko tod dega. Mobile design hamesha *alag se* banaya jaata hai (e.g., 12 column se 4 column mein content ko manually adjust karke). 'Scale' tool ka use sirf illustrations ya vectors (jo pixel-perfect na hon) ko scale karne ke liye hota hai.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Professionals 'Scale Tool' (K) ko UI par *kabhi* use nahi karte. Woh illustrations, icons, ya non-UI elements ko scale karne ke liye use karte hain. Responsive design (Desktop to Mobile) *hamesha* Auto Layout (Fill Container, Hug) aur Layout Grids (12-col to 4-col) ka use karke *manually* banaya jaata hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example (Viewport):** Aapne mobile app (375px) design ki. Aap 'Present' (Play) dabate hain. Aapki monitor screen 1920px hai. Agar Viewport `100%` hoga, toh app choti si dikhegi. Agar `Fit to Screen` hoga, toh app (aur iPhone frame) zoom hokar aapki screen par fit ho jayenge.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * **'Scale Tool' (K) ko UI Frames par *mat* use karein.** Yeh aapke grid aur font sizes ko tod dega.
    * Illustrations ya complex vectors ko scale karne ke liye `K` use karein.
    * Responsive design (Desktop/Mobile) ke liye Auto Layout (Resizing) aur Constraints use karein.
    * Prototype present karte waqt hamesha 'Viewport' ko `Fit to Screen` (ya 'Fit') par rakhein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **'Scale' (K) aur 'Move' (V) mein kya fark hai?** `V` (Move) se Frame resize karne par andar ka content *nahi* badalta. `K` (Scale) se Frame resize karne par *andar ka content* (font, stroke, etc.) bhi badal jaata hai.
    * **Mera prototype bohot bada/chota dikh raha hai!** Top-right mein 'Options' -> 'Viewport' ko 'Fit to Screen' karein.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. Ek Frame (Button) banayein (Text 16px, Padding 16px).
    * 2. Use `V` (Move tool) se bada karein. (Dekhein, text 16px hi raha).
    * 3. Use `K` (Scale tool) se bada karein. (Dekhein, text bhi 16px se bada ho gaya).
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * (N/A)

---

### 4.8: Mobile-Specific Design (Touch Targets)

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Mobile-Specific Design (Touch Targets) ğŸ“±ğŸ‘† (Ungli se click karne laayak design).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Touch Target woh invisible area hota hai ek element (jaise button, icon, link) ka jispar user apni *ungli* (finger) se tap (click) kar sakta hai. Mobile-specific design yeh sunishchit (ensure) karta hai ki yeh targets itne bade hon ki unhe aasaani se tap kiya jaa sake.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Kyunki mobile par hum mouse (jo 1px ka hota hai) nahi, balki ungli (jo ~44px ki hoti hai) use karte hain. Agar aapke buttons (touch targets) bohot chote (e.g., 20px) ya ek doosre se bohot chipke hue honge, toh user galti se 'Delete' ki jagah 'Save' daba dega. Yeh 'Usability' (upyogita) ka sabse important rule hai.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab bhi aap mobile app ya mobile website (touchscreen ke liye) design kar rahe hon. Har button, har icon, har link design karte waqt. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh 'Fat Finger Problem' (galtiyan se galat cheez tap ho jaana) ko solve karta hai.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapka app 'unusable' (istemal na karne laayak) hoga. Users frustrate ho jayenge kyunki woh sahi button nahi daba payenge. Aapka app 'App Store' ya 'Play Store' ki accessibility guidelines ko fail kar dega.
6.  **ğŸ§‘_ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown (The Rules):**_
    * **Apple (iOS Guidelines):** Recommended minimum touch target `44px` by `44px` hai.
    * **Google (Material Design):** Recommended minimum touch target `48dp` by `48dp` hai (jo ~48px hai).
    * **Rule of Thumb:** **Aapka koi bhi clickable element (button, icon button) `40px` height se chota *nahi* hona chahiye.** `44px` ya `48px` (8-point grid ke hisaab se) best hai.
    * **Spacing:** Do touch targets (e.g., 'Save' aur 'Cancel' button) ke beech *kam se kam* `8px` ki spacing honi chahiye.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek 'Icon Button' (jaise 'Back' arrow) banana jo touch-friendly ho.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Aap 'Feather Icons' plugin se ek 'Arrow-Left' icon laayein (woh `24px` ka hoga).
        2.  Agar aapne sirf is 24px icon ko clickable banaya, toh yeh bohot chota hai.
        3.  **Sahi Tareeka:** Icon (24px) ko select karein.
        4.  `Shift+A` (Auto Layout) dabayein.
        5.  `Horizontal padding` ko `12px` set karein.
        6.  `Vertical padding` ko `12px` set karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapke paas ab ek *container* (Auto Layout Frame) hai jiska size `48px` by `48px` hai (24px icon + 12px left/right + 12px top/bottom). Bhale hi icon *dikhne* mein 24px ka hai, uska *clickable area* (touch target) 48px ka hai. Yeh perfect hai.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * Desktop design (jahan buttons 32px height ke ho sakte hain) ko seedha mobile par copy-paste kar dena.
    * Icons (jo aksar 24px ke hote hain) ko hi clickable bana dena, unke chaaron taraf padding (touch area) add kiye bina.
    * Do buttons (e.g., 'Like' aur 'Comment') ko ekdum chipka dena (0px spacing).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Mera icon 24px ka hai, par main button 44px ka banaunga toh design ajeeb (khaali) nahi lagega?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Yahi 4.8 ka example hai. Icon 24px ka hi *dikhega*. Lekin hum `Shift+A` (Auto Layout) se uske chaaron taraf *invisible* padding daal kar uske 'Frame' (container) ko 44px ya 48px ka banayenge. Developer is poore 'Frame' ko clickable banayega.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Design System mein, 'Icon Button' component ka *minimum size* hi 44x44px (ya 48x48px) set hota hai. Icon (24px) uske andar center-aligned hota hai. Koi bhi designer isse chota button bana hi nahi sakta.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Apne phone par koi bhi app (Instagram, Gmail) kholein. 'Back' button, 'Like' button, ya 'Profile' tab... bhale hi icon chota dikhe, unka clickable area (touch target) 44px se zyada hi hota hai.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Mobile design mein *har* clickable element ki minimum height `40px` rakhein. `44px` ya `48px` ideal hai.
    * Do clickable elements ke beech *kam se kam* `8px` ki spacing rakhein.
    * Chote icons (24px) ke chaaron taraf Auto Layout se 'padding' add karke unka touch target bada karein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Kya desktop par bhi 44px zaroori hai?** Nahi. Desktop par mouse hota hai, isliye wahan buttons chote ho sakte hain (e.g., 32px, 36px height). Lekin consistency ke liye, bohot si teams 40px+ hi rakhti hain.
    * **Text Links (jaise 'Forgot Password?') ka kya karein?** Unka bhi touch target bada hona chahiye. Bhale hi font size 14px ho, unke 'Frame' (Auto Layout) ki 'vertical padding' badha kar total height 40px+ kar dein.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. Ek 24px ka 'Settings' (gear) icon lein.
    * 2. Use Auto Layout (Shift+A) ka istemaal karke uska total size (touch target) 48x48px karein (bina icon ka size badle).
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Apple Human Interface Guidelines (Accessibility):** Touch Targets par search karein.
    * **Google Material Design (Accessibility):** Touch Targets par search karein.

---

Whew! ğŸ¥µ Yeh ek lamba aur heavy module tha, par aapne ab Figma ka 70% power seekh liya hai. Auto Layout aur Constraints mein mastery hi aapko job-ready banayegi.

Jab aap ready hon, bas **"Module 5 shuru karo"** likh dena, aur hum 'Design Systems' (Reusable Styles aur Effects) ki duniya mein kadam rakhenge!


=============================================================

Chalo bhai, shuru karte hain aapke Figma (Beginner-to-Job-Ready) notes ka Module 5!

Module 4 mein humne 'Layout' (haddiyon ka dhancha) master kiya. Ab Module 5 mein hum 'Visual Polish' (skin aur look) par focus karenge. Yahan hum 'Design Systems' ki neenv (foundation) rakhenge. Yeh seekhna bohot zaroori hai taaki aapka design *scalable* (bada karne laayak) aur *consistent* (ek jaisa) ban sake.

### 5.1: Creating Color & Text Styles (Global Styles)

**(Yeh ek CORE Foundational topic hai. Poora dhyaan dein.)**

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Color & Text Styles (Global Styles) ğŸ¨ (Apne design ke 'Atoms' banana).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Styles 'reusable properties' (baar-baar istemaal hone waale gun) hote hain. Yeh aapko apne colors (e.g., brand ka blue color) aur text properties (e.g., 'Heading 1' font) ko *save* karke, poori file mein kahin bhi *ek click se* apply karne dete hain.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh **consistency** aur **speed** ke liye sabse zaroori hai. Yeh 'Atomic Design' (Module 2) ka 'Atom' level hai. Isse aapko har baar Blue color ka Hex code (`#0D99FF`) yaad nahi rakhna padta.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Project shuru karte hi! Wireframes ke baad aur High-Fidelity design se pehle. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Sabse badi problem: "Client ne kaha 'Blue color thoda dark kar do'." Agar aapne Styles use nahi kiye, toh aapko 100 jagah jaakar manually (haath se) color badalna padega. Agar Style use kiya hai, toh aap *ek jagah* Style ko edit karenge, aur poori file mein jahan-jahan woh style (color) use hua hai, woh *automatically update* ho jayega.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapka design inconsistent hoga (kahin light blue, kahin dark blue). Aapka bohot saara time waste hoga. Aapka design 'scalable' nahi hoga. Ek chota sa color change karna bhi ek 'dard' (pain) ban jayega.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Creating a Style:** Aap ek element (Text ya Shape) ko style (e.g., Red color) dete hain.
    * **Right Panel:** 'Fill' (color ke liye) ya 'Text' section mein, 4-dot (Style) icon âˆ· par click karein.
    * **`+` (Create Style):** `+` icon par click karein, naam dein (e.g., "Brand/Primary-Blue"), aur 'Create Style' karein.
    * **Applying a Style:** Ab naya element banayein. 'Fill' (ya Text) ke 4-dot icon âˆ· par click karein aur list se apna save kiya hua "Primary-Blue" style chunein.
    * **Editing a Style:** Canvas par *kuch bhi select na karein*. Right Panel mein aapko apne saare local styles dikhenge. Wahan se edit karein.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek 'Primary Button' color style aur 'Heading 1' text style banana.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation (Color Style):**
        1.  Ek Rectangle `(R)` banayein.
        2.  Right Panel mein 'Fill' se use ek Blue color (`#0D99FF`) dein.
        3.  'Fill' section mein 4-dot âˆ· (Style) icon par click karein.
        4.  Panel mein `+` (Create Style) par click karein.
        5.  Naam rakhein: `Brand/Primary` (Slash `/` use karne se 'Brand' naam ka folder ban jayega).
        6.  'Create Style' dabayein.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation (Text Style):**
        1.  Ek Text `(T)` likhein.
        2.  Right Panel mein Text properties set karein: Font 'Inter', Weight 'Bold', Size '32px'.
        3.  'Text' section mein 4-dot âˆ· (Style) icon par click karein.
        4.  `+` (Create Style) par click karein.
        5.  Naam rakhein: `Headings/H1`.
        6.  'Create Style' dabayein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Ab aap canvas par kahin bhi click (deselect) karenge, toh Right Panel par aapko 'Color Styles' mein 'Brand/Primary' aur 'Text Styles' mein 'Headings/H1' dikhega.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * Styles ka istemaal hi na karna. (Sabse badi galti).
    * Har chote-mote color (e.g., 5 alag-alag grey shades) ka style bana dena. (Sirf unka banayein jo reusable hon, jaise Primary, Secondary, Text, Background, Error).
    * Naam theek se na dena (`Color 1`, `Text Style 5`). Hamesha clear naam dein (e.g., `Color/Brand/Primary`, `Font/Body/Regular-16`). Slash `/` se naming (folder structure) bohot zaroori hai.
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main toh bas copy-paste karke (Alt-drag) ya 'Eyedropper' tool (i) se color copy kar sakta hoon. Styles kyun?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Copy-paste 'link' (connection) nahi banata. Agar aapne 50 jagah blue button copy-paste kiya aur client ne color change ko kaha, toh aapko 50 baar edit karna padega. Agar aapne 'Style' use kiya hota, toh aap *Style* ko edit karte aur 50 ke 50 buttons 1 second mein update ho jaate.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Design Team 'Design System' file mein pehle *sirf* Styles (Atoms) define karti hai. (e.g., Primary colors, Neutral greys, H1, H2, Body text). Phir woh in styles ko 'Publish' (publish) karti hai library mein. Doosre designers un styles ko *use* karte hain, edit nahi kar sakte. Isse poori company ke 100+ products mein consistency rehti hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Twitter/X ka brand color blue se 'Black' hua. Designers ne *ek* 'Primary' color style ko (blue se black) update kiya, aur poori app (har button, har link, har icon) automatically update ho gayi.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Hamesha Styles use karein (Colors, Text, Effects).
    * Clear naming convention use karein (e.g., `Category/Item` ya `Category/Sub-Category/Item`).
    * Apne styles ko canvas par (deselect karke) Right Panel se manage karein.
    * Har cheez ka style na banayein. Sirf 'System' ka hissa (reusable items) ka banayein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Style ko delete/edit kaise karein?** Canvas par 'Esc' dabayein (taaki kuch select na ho). Right panel mein jo style list dikhe, wahan style par right-click karke 'Edit' ya 'Delete' karein.
    * **Style ko 'detach' (hatana) kaise karein?** Ek element (jispar style laga hai) ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'Fill' (ya Text) section mein style ke naam ke paas 'Detach' (toota hua link) ğŸ”— icon par click karein.
    * **Main 'Gradient' (multiple colors) ka style bana sakta hoon?** Haan! Bilkul color style ki tarah hi, gradient fill banakar 4-dot icon âˆ· se save karein.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. Ek 'Error/Red' color style banayein.
    * 2. Ek 'Body/Regular' text style banayein (e.g., Inter, Regular, 16px).
    * 3. Ek 'Primary/Green' color style banayein aur use *edit* karke 'Primary/Purple' karein (aur dekhein ki woh element par update hota hai ya nahi).
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Design Systems (Module 7):** Yeh concept 'Team Libraries' ke saath judkar aur powerful ho jaata hai.
    * **Variables (Module 7):** Yeh Styles ka bhi advanced version hain (jo hum aage dekhenge).

---

### 5.2: Effects (Shadows, Blurs)

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Effects (Shadows, Blurs) âœ¨ (Depth aur Glassmorphism banana).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** 'Effects' Right Panel mein ek section hai jo aapko ek layer par visual effects (jaise parchhayi ya dhundhlapan) daalne deta hai.
    * **Drop Shadow (Parchhayi):** Element ke *neeche* parchhayi daalta hai. Isse element 'z-axis' (uppar utha hua) dikhta hai.
    * **Inner Shadow:** Element ke *andar* parchhayi daalta hai (jaise ek 'daba hua' button).
    * **Layer Blur (Dhundhlapan):** Poore element (shape, image) ko dhundhla (blur) kar deta hai.
    * **Background Blur:** Element ke *aar-paar* (through) dikhne waali cheezon ko blur kar deta hai. (Yeh 'Glassmorphism' effect ke liye zaroori hai).
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh aapke 'flat' (sapaat) design ko depth (gehrai) aur visual interest deta hai. 'Drop Shadow' se pata chalta hai ki kaun sa element (e.g., Pop-up Modal) baaki content ke uppar hai. 'Background Blur' se modern 'glass' jaisa effect banta hai.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):**
    * **Drop Shadow:** Cards, Buttons (hover effect), Modals, Pop-ups.
    * **Layer Blur:** Jab ek image ko background mein 'out of focus' dikhana ho.
    * **Background Blur:** Frosted glass waale sidebars, navbars, ya modals banane ke liye.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapka design bohot 'flat' aur 'boring' lag sakta hai. Hierarchy (kaun uppar hai, kaun neeche) clear nahi hogi. Aap modern UI effects (jaise glassmorphism) nahi bana payenge.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Apply:** Element select karein -> Right Panel mein 'Effects' par `+` dabayein.
    * **Select:** Default 'Drop Shadow' aayega. Uske naam par click karke 'Layer Blur' etc. chunein.
    * **Settings (Effect icon â˜€ï¸):** Har effect ke paas â˜€ï¸ icon hota hai.
        * **Drop Shadow Settings:**
            * `X`: Parchhayi left/right kitni door.
            * `Y`: Parchhayi upar/neeche kitni door (e.g., `4px` neeche).
            * `Blur`: Parchhayi kitni 'soft' (dhundhli) hai (e.g., `12px`).
            * `Spread`: Parchhayi kitni 'faili' hui hai (aksar `0` rakhte hain).
            * `Color (Opacity)`: Parchhayi ka color (hamesha Black `000` use karein, par opacity `10%` se `25%` rakhein, 100% black nahi!).
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task 1:** Ek 'Card' par soft shadow lagana.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Ek Rectangle (Card) banayein (Fill: White).
        2.  Right Panel mein 'Effects' par `+` dabayein.
        3.  Effect (Drop Shadow) ke paas â˜€ï¸ icon par click karein.
        4.  Settings: `X: 0`, `Y: 4`, `Blur: 12`, `Spread: 0`.
        5.  Color: `000000` (Black) chunein, par uski Opacity (slider) ko `15%` kar dein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Card ke neeche ek bohot 'soft' aur 'natural' dikhne waali parchhayi aa jayegi.
    * **Task 2 (Glassmorphism):**
        1.  Background mein ek colorful image rakhein.
        2.  Uske upar ek Rectangle banayein.
        3.  Rectangle ka 'Fill' `White` karein aur opacity `20%` kar dein.
        4.  'Effects' mein `+` dabayein. 'Drop Shadow' ki jagah `Background Blur` chunein.
        5.  â˜€ï¸ Settings mein Blur amount ko `40px` kar dein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapka rectangle 'frosted glass' jaisa ban jayega, aur uske neeche ki image blur dikhegi.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * Default (100% black, 0 blur) waali 'hard' (sakht) shadow use karna, jo bohot gandi (ugly) dikhti hai. **Rule: Hamesha shadow ko 'Blur' dein aur 'Opacity' kam karein.**
    * 'Layer Blur' (jo element ko blur karta hai) aur 'Background Blur' (jo element ke *peeche* blur karta hai) mein confuse hona.
    * Bahut zyada ya bahut dark shadow use karna. (Subtle = Professional).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main 'Drop Shadow' ka 'Style' âˆ· (jaise color ka) bana sakta hoon?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Haan! Bilkul color ki tarah. Ek student 2-3 shadow styles banata hai: `Shadow/Small` (button hover ke liye), `Shadow/Medium` (card ke liye), `Shadow/Large` (Modal/Pop-up ke liye). Ab usse har baar Y/Blur/Opacity yaad nahi rakhni padti.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Design System mein 'Elevation' (uthhaav) ke naam se shadow styles hote hain. (e.g., `Elevation-0` (koi shadow nahi), `Elevation-1` (small shadow), `Elevation-2` (medium shadow)). Developers in styles ko seedha CSS code mein use karte hain.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** macOS/Windows 11 ka interface, jahan Sidebars aur Taskbar 'Background Blur' (Glassmorphism) ka bohot use karte hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Hamesha 'soft' shadows use karein (Blur zyada, Opacity kam).
    * 'Background Blur' ke liye, layer ki 'Fill' opacity ko bhi kam (e.g., 10-30%) karna zaroori hai.
    * Apne sabse common shadows (e.g., Card Shadow) ko 'Effect Style' âˆ· bana kar save kar lein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Main ek element par 2 shadow (e.g., ek choti, ek badi) laga sakta hoon?** Haan! 'Effects' section mein `+` daba kar ek aur 'Drop Shadow' add karein. Yeh realistic shadows ke liye advanced technique hai.
    * **Mera Background Blur kaam nahi kar raha!** Check karein ki (1) aapke layer (rectangle) ki 'Fill' opacity 100% se kam hai, aur (2) uske *peeche* koi aur layer (e.g., image) hai jisse woh blur kar sake.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Card shadow' waali exercise (Task 1) ko dobara karein.
    * 2. 'Glassmorphism' waali exercise (Task 2) ko dobara karein.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Smooth Shadow (Plugin):** Bohat hi smooth, layered shadows (jaise CSS mein bante hain) banane ke liye.

---

### 5.3: Blending Modes

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Blending Modes (Layers ko mix karna).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Blending Mode (Photoshop users ko pata hoga) yeh control karta hai ki ek layer (uppar waali) apne *neeche* waali layer ke pixels (colors) ke saath kaise 'interact' (mix) karti hai. Yeh Right Panel mein 'Layer' section (jahan Opacity 100% likha hota hai) mein milta hai.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh advanced visual effects ke liye zaroori hai. Isse aap images par 'color tint' (rang chadhana) ya 'vignette' (corners dark karna) jaise effects bana sakte hain, jo simple 'Opacity' se nahi ban sakte.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab aapko 2 layers (aksar ek Image aur ek Color layer) ko artistically blend (mix) karna ho.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Koi badi problem nahi hogi (yeh advanced topic hai). Par aap kuch popular design effects (jaise 'Duotone' images ya 'Color Burn') nahi bana payenge.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown (Common Modes):**
    * **Pass-through (Default for Frames):** Frame ke andar ke elements ka blend mode use hota hai.
    * **Normal (Default for Layers):** Uppar waali layer neeche waali ko bas dhak leti hai (opacity ke hisaab se).
    * **Multiply:** Dono layers ke colors ko 'multiply' (guna) karta hai. Result hamesha *darker* (gehra) hota hai. (White color `Multiply` mein gayab ho jaata hai).
    * **Screen:** Multiply ka ulta. Result hamesha *lighter* (halka) hota hai. (Black color `Screen` mein gayab ho jaata hai).
    * **Overlay / Soft Light:** Yeh 'Multiply' (dark) aur 'Screen' (light) ka combination hai. Yeh image ka 'contrast' badhaane ke liye best hai.
    * **Color:** Uppar waali layer ka 'Hue' (rang) aur 'Saturation' (teevrata) le leta hai, aur neeche waali layer ki 'Luminance' (brightness) rakhta hai. (Image ko Black & White karke uspe rang chadhane ke liye).
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek 'Image' ko brand ke 'Blue' color se tint (rangeen) karna.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Neeche ek 'Image' layer rakhein (e.g., ek black & white portrait photo).
        2.  Uske *uppar* ek 'Rectangle' (shape) banayein, jo image ko poora dhak le.
        3.  Rectangle ka 'Fill' apne brand 'Blue' color se karein.
        4.  Ab is Blue Rectangle (uppar waali layer) ko select karein.
        5.  Right Panel mein 'Layer' section mein, 'Blending' (jahan 'Normal' likha hai) ko badal kar `Multiply` ya `Color` ya `Overlay` karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Image aur blue color aapas mein 'mix' ho jayenge. 'Multiply' se image 'dark blue' tint legi. 'Color' se image 'blue' (par original brightness ke saath) ho jayegi.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * Blend modes ko `Fill` section (andar) aur `Layer` section (poori layer) mein confuse karna. (Aksar `Layer` waala hi use hota hai).
    * Har blend mode ko try karke time waste karna. (90% time aap sirf `Multiply`, `Screen`, aur `Overlay` hi use karenge).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main 'Fill' ki opacity kam karke bhi toh tint de sakta hoon? Iski kya zaroorat hai?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Opacity kam karne se image 'dhundhli' (washed out) lagti hai. 'Multiply' (ya `Overlay`) use karne se image ke 'details' (shadows/highlights) zinda rehte hain aur color 'rich' (gehra) lagta hai.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Brand identity mein iska use hota hai. Jaise Spotify 'Duotone' image effect (2 colors ko blend karna) ke liye famous tha.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Ek image ke upar 'Hero Section' mein text (White color) padhna mushkil hai. Image ke upar ek 'Black' rectangle daalein aur uska blend mode `Multiply` (ya `Soft Light`) aur opacity `40%` kar dein. Image dark ho jayegi aur text clear padha jayega. (Yeh Masking/Gradient se alag technique hai).
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Image ko dark tint dene ke liye: Black Layer + `Multiply` (ya `Overlay`) + Opacity (30-60%).
    * Image ko light tint dene ke liye: White Layer + `Screen` (ya `Soft Light`) + Opacity (30-60%).
    * Image ko colorize karne ke liye: Color Layer + `Color` (ya `Overlay`).
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **`Pass-through` (jo Frame par default hai) ka kya matlab hai?** Iska matlab hai ki Frame khud blend nahi hoga, par *andar* ke elements blend honge. Agar aapne Frame ka blend mode 'Normal' kar diya, toh poora Frame ek 'flat' image ki tarah blend hoga.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Image ko Blue tint' waali exercise (Task) ko dobara karein aur `Multiply`, `Overlay`, `Color` modes try karke fark dekhein.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * (Yeh Photoshop/Illustrator ka core concept hai).

---

### 5.4: Background Styles & Fills

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Background Styles & Fills (Solid, Gradient, Image).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):**
    * **Fill (Right Panel):** Yeh *kisi bhi* layer (Shape, Text, Frame) ke andar ka content hai. Yeh `Solid` color, `Gradient` (Linear, Radial, etc.), ya `Image` (Topic 3.1) ho sakta hai.
    * **Background (Right Panel):** Yeh *sirf* 'Frame' ki property hoti hai. Yeh 'Fill' jaisa hi hai, par yeh Frame ke 'background' ka color hota hai.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh aapke design ka base (aadhaar) hai. 'Fill' se aap buttons banate hain, 'Background' se aap poori screen ka background set karte hain. 'Gradients' (ek color se doosre mein smooth transition) aapke design ko modern aur energetic look dete hain.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):**
    * **Fill:** Har element (Button, Card, Text) ko color dene ke liye.
    * **Background:** Poori Screen (Frame) ka background color set karne ke liye.
    * **Gradients:** Buttons, Cards, aur khaaskar Hero Section (backgrounds) ko attractive banane ke liye.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapka design 'transparent' (paardarshi) ya 'white' hi reh jayega.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Multiple Fills:** Aap ek hi element par `+` daba kar *ek se zyada* fills laga sakte hain. (e.g., Neeche 'Image' fill, uske uppar 'Gradient' fill).
    * **Gradient (Fill property):**
        1.  'Fill' par click karein. Top-left par 'Solid' ki jagah `Linear` (ya `Radial`, `Angular`, `Diamond`) chunein.
        2.  Aapko ek 'gradient bar' dikhega.
        3.  Pehle color 'stop' (box) ko chunein, color dein (e.g., Blue).
        4.  Doosre color 'stop' ko chunein, color dein (e.g., Purple).
        5.  Aap bar ko (canvas par) rotate karke gradient ka angle badal sakte hain.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek 'Login Button' par 'Linear Gradient' Fill lagana.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Ek Button (Auto Layout Frame, text ke saath) banayein.
        2.  Frame ko select karein. 'Fill' par `+` dabayein.
        3.  'Fill' panel kholein. 'Solid' ki jagah `Linear` chunein.
        4.  Pehla color stop (left waala): `Blue` chunein, Opacity 100%.
        5.  Doosra color stop (right waala): `Light Blue` (ya `Purple`) chunein, Opacity 100%.
        6.  Canvas par gradient bar dikhega. Uske handles ko 'top-left' se 'bottom-right' tak drag karein taaki gradient diagonal (tirchha) ho jaaye.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapke paas ek sundar, modern gradient waala button hoga.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * **'Fill' aur 'Background' (Frame par) mein confuse hona.** Rule: 'Fill' sabke liye hai. 'Background' sirf Frame ke liye hai. (Aksar log Frame ke liye 'Fill' hi use karte hain, 'Background' property ko chhod dete hain. Dono se ek hi result milta hai).
    * Bohat 'loud' (tez) ya 'ajeeb' (clashing) colors ke gradients banana.
    * Gradient mein ek color ko transparent (0% Opacity) kar dena, jisse woh 'fade' effect ban jaata hai (jo kabhi-kabhi zaroori hota hai).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main 'Gradient' ka 'Style' âˆ· (jaise solid color ka) bana sakta hoon?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Haan! Bilkul. Ek student apne brand ka 'Primary Gradient' (Blue-to-Purple) style save kar leta hai. Ab woh har 'Primary Button' par 1-click mein woh gradient laga sakta hai.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Design System mein 'Gradient Styles' bhi hote hain. (e.g., `Gradient/Brand`, `Gradient/Neutral`). Isse saare buttons aur hero sections par consistent gradients rehte hain.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Instagram ka puraana logo 'Radial Gradient' (center se nikalne waala) tha. Stripe, Apple, aur bohot si modern companies apne marketing materials mein 'Linear Gradients' ka bharpoor istemaal karti hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Apne gradients ko 'subtle' (halka) rakhein. (Doosra color pehle waale se thoda milta-julta ho).
    * Apne reusable gradients ko 'Color Style' bana kar save karein.
    * Ek hi element par multiple fills (e.g., Image + Gradient overlay) ka use karna seekhein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Main ek element par color aur image, dono fill kaise karun?** 'Fill' section mein `+` dabayein. Pehla fill 'Image' chunein. Phir `+` dabakar doosra fill 'Solid' (e.g., Black) chunein. Is Black fill ko image ke *uppar* rakhein (drag karke) aur uski opacity 50% kar dein. (Yeh 'image overlay' ban gaya).
    * **Frame ka 'Fill' aur 'Background' mein kya fark hai?** 'Fill' hamesha 'Layout Grids' (Module 4) ke *uppar* dikhta hai. 'Background' hamesha 'Layout Grids' ke *peeche* dikhta hai. (99% log 'Fill' hi use karte hain).
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Gradient Button' waali exercise (Task) ko dobara karein.
    * 2. Ek Rectangle banayein. Usmein 2 Fills daalein: (1) Neeche 'Image' fill, (2) Upar 'Linear Gradient' (Black 80% to Transparent 0%) fill. (Yeh ek 'text protection' gradient banayega, jiske upar white text clear dikhega).
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **uiGradients (Website):** Sundar gradients ke ideas lene ke liye.
    * **Noise (Plugin):** Apne fills/gradients mein thoda 'texture' (noise) add karne ke liye.

---

Yeh tha hamara Module 5! ğŸ¨ Aapne 'Styles' (Atoms) banana seekh liya hai, jisse aapka kaam tez aur consistent hoga. Aapne shadows, blurs, aur gradients se design ko 'polished' (sundar) banana bhi seekh liya hai.

Aapka Design System ka base ready hai.

Jab aap ready hon, bas **"Module 6 shuru karo"** likh dena, aur hum Design Systems ke agle aur sabse zaroori kadam: **Components (Reusable elements)** mein dive karenge!

=============================================================

Chalo bhai, shuru karte hain aapke Figma (Beginner-to-Job-Ready) notes ka Module 6!

Prompt aapka saved hai, boss! Main aapke nirdeshon ke hisaab se hi chalunga.

Yeh module hamare 'Design System' ka Part 2 hai. Module 5 mein humne 'Atoms' (Styles) banaye. Ab Module 6 mein hum 'Molecules' aur 'Organisms' (Components) banana seekhenge. Yeh Figma ka **doosra sabse zaroori feature** hai (Auto Layout ke baad). Poora dhyaan dena!

### 6.1: Creating Components

**(Yeh ek CORE Foundational topic hai. Poora dhyaan dein.)**

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Creating Components ğŸ§© (Reusable design elements banana).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Component ek 'Master' (mukhya) design element hai jise aap ek baar banate hain (e.g., ek 'Button'), aur phir uski 'Instances' (copies) ko poore design mein *reuse* (baar-baar istemaal) kar sakte hain.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh **scalability** aur **consistency** ki chaabi (key) hai. Jab aap 'Master Component' (e.g., master button) ko update karte hain (jaise uska color badalte hain), toh uski *saari* 100 'Instances' (copies) poore app mein jahan bhi use hui hain, woh *automatically* ek saath update ho jaati hain.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** **Jab bhi aap koi element (UI ka hissa) ek se zyada baar use karne waale hon.** Jaise: Buttons, Icons, Navbar, Footer, Product Cards, List Items... sab kuch. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh us problem ko solve karta hai jahan aapne 100 'Buy Now' button copy-paste kiye, aur client ne kaha, "Button ka color Blue se Green kar do." Components ke bina, aapko 100 jagah jaakar haath se (manually) color change karna padega. Component ke saath, aap 1 jagah change karenge aur 1 second mein kaam ho jayega.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** **Aapka workflow barbaad ho jayega.** Aapka design inconsistent (alag-alag) hoga. Aapka bohot (bohot!) zyada time waste hoga simple changes karne mein. Aapka design 'scalable' (bada karne laayak) nahi hoga. Developers aapse nafrat karenge kyunki aapne 10 alag-alag button design (jo ek jaise dikhte hain) diye honge, jabki unhe *ek* hi reusable code component banana tha. Bina components ke, aap professional designer nahi kehla sakte.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Main Component (Master):** Yeh original design hai. Layers Panel mein iska icon â– (chaar diamond) hota hai. Ise hamesha ek alag 'Components' page par rakha jaata hai.
    * **Instance (Copy):** Yeh component ki 'linked copy' (judi hui copy) hai. Layers Panel mein iska icon â™¢ (khaali diamond) hota hai. Instances ko aap design screens (e.g., Home page) par use karte hain.
    * **Overrides (Badlaav):** Aap 'Instance' par chote-mote badlaav (jaise text badalna, color badalna) kar sakte hain. Yeh badlaav sirf uss *ek* instance par laagu hote hain, 'Master' par nahi.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek reusable 'Primary Button' component banana.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Sabse pehle, Module 1.2 ke anusaar, ek naya 'Page' ğŸ—ƒï¸ banayein aur use naam dein "ğŸ§© Components". Hum saare masters yahan rakhenge.
        2.  Is page par, hamara Auto Layout (Module 4.4) waala button banayein:
        3.  `T` daba kar "Button Text" likhein.
        4.  `Shift+A` daba kar Auto Layout add karein.
        5.  Padding set karein (e.g., Horizontal 24px, Vertical 16px).
        6.  'Fill' mein hamara 'Brand/Primary' (Module 5.1) waala color style apply karein.
        7.  'Text' mein hamara 'Font/Button' waala text style apply karein.
        8.  **Yeh Kadam Zaroori Hai:** Is Auto Layout Frame (Button) ko select karein.
        9.  Toolbar (top-center) mein 4-dot â– (Create Component) icon par click karein. (Shortcut: `Ctrl+Alt+K` ya `Cmd+Opt+K`).
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapka button 'purple' color ka ho jayega aur Layers Panel mein uska icon â– (master component) ban jayega. Aapne apna pehla component bana liya hai!
    * **Using it:** Ab apni design waali 'ğŸ“± High-Fidelity' page par jaayein. 'Assets' panel (Left Panel) mein dekhein. Aapko "Components" page ke andar "Button Text" (jo bhi naam tha) dikhega. Usse *drag-and-drop* karke apne design frame (e.g., iPhone frame) mein laayein. Yeh ek 'Instance' (â™¢) hai.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * **Master component ko hi design (e.g., Home page) mein use kar lena.** (Galat! Master hamesha 'Components' page par rehna chahiye. Aap hamesha 'Instance' (copy) ko hi design mein use karein).
    * **Component banane ke baad Master ko delete kar dena.** (Master delete, toh saare instances 'toot' (detach) jaayenge).
    * Har choti cheez (jaise ek simple 'Rectangle') ka component bana dena. (Sirf *reusable* cheezon ka banayein).
    * Component banane se *pehle* Auto Layout (`Shift+A`) ka istemaal na karna. (Aap kar sakte hain, par Auto Layout + Component = Super flexible component).
    * 'Instance' ko *edit* karne ki koshish karna. (Aap Instance par 'Overrides' kar sakte hain, par structural changes (jaise icon add karna) hamesha 'Master' â– mein hi hote hain).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main toh bas 'Alt-drag' (duplicate) karke button copy kar sakta hoon. Component (itna jhanjhat) kyun?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Woh "Alt-drag" (duplicate) 10 copies banata hai jo ek doosre se 'unlinked' (judi hui nahi) hain. 'Instance' (drag from Assets) 10 copies banata hai jo 'Master' se 'linked' (judi hui) hain. Jab aapko 10 buttons ka corner radius 8px se 40px (poora gol) karna hoga, tab aapko 'Component' ki power samajh aayegi (1-second update).
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Ek 'Design System' file hoti hai jismein *sirf* Master Components (â–) hote hain. Woh file 'Library' ki tarah 'Publish' hoti hai (Module 7). Baaki saare designers (jo alag-alag product files mein kaam kar rahe hain) un components ki 'Instances' (â™¢) ko use karte hain. Jab 'Design System' team 'Master Button' ka color badalti hai, toh company ke *saare* products mein woh button *automatically* update ho jaata hai. Yahi hai scalability.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Ek e-commerce app mein 'Product Card' (Image, Title, Price, Buy Button) ek *component* hota hai. Search results page par wohi component 20 baar (instance) use hota hai. Agar 'Price' ka font size badalna hai, toh designer 'Master Product Card' component mein 1 jagah change karta hai, aur 20 ke 20 cards update ho jaate hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * **DRY: Don't Repeat Yourself.** Agar aap koi cheez copy-paste kar rahe hain, ruk jaao! Uska 'Component' â– banao.
    * Apne saare 'Master' components (â–) ko ek alag 'ğŸ§© Components' Page par rakho.
    * Components ko hamesha 'Auto Layout' (`Shift+A`) ke saath combine karke banao.
    * Clear naam do (e.g., `Button/Primary/Default`). Slash `/` se Assets panel mein folder ban jaate hain.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Master component (jo 'Components' page par hai) ko dhoondhoon kaise?** Kisi bhi 'Instance' (â™¢) par right-click karein -> 'Go to Main Component'.
    * **Instance ka Master se link kaise todein?** Instance (â™¢) par right-click karein -> 'Detach Instance'. (Ab yeh ek normal frame/group ban gaya hai).
    * **Instance par kiye gaye badlaav (overrides) ko reset kaise karein?** Instance (â™¢) ko select karein. Right Panel mein instance ke naam ke paas `...` (more) icon par click karein -> 'Reset all overrides'.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Primary Button' waali exercise (Task) ko poora karein.
    * 2. Ek 'Navbar' (Logo + Links + Button) ka poora 'Horizontal Auto Layout' banayein aur use *ek* component (â–) mein convert karein.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Variants (Topic 6.2):** Component ki agli superpower.

---

### 6.2: Component Variants

**(Yeh ek CORE Foundational topic hai. Poora dhyaan dein.)**

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Component Variants (Ek component ke alag-alag roop).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Variants (vigyapan) aapko *ek hi* component ke alag-alag 'states' (avasthaayein) ya 'versions' (roop) ko *ek group* mein combine karne deta hai. Jaise, ek 'Button' component ke 4 variants ho sakte hain: `Default`, `Hover`, `Pressed`, `Disabled`.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh aapke 'Assets Panel' (component library) ko *saaf-suthra* (clean) rakhta hai. Iske bina, aapko 4 alag-alag component banane padenge (`Button/Default` â–, `Button/Hover` â–, `Button/Pressed` â–...). Variants ke saath, aapke paas *sirf ek* component hota hai ('Button' â–), aur uski properties (gun) aap Right Panel se 'switch' (badal) sakte hain (e.g., "State: Default" se "State: Hover" karna).
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab bhi aapka ek component 2 ya 2 se zyada 'states' (avastha) ya 'types' (prakaar) ka ho.
    * **Examples:**
        * **Button:** States (Default, Hover, Disabled), Types (Primary, Secondary).
        * **Input Field:** States (Default, Focused, Error).
        * **Icon:** Types (Small, Medium, Large).
    * Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh "Component Overload" (Assets panel mein 50 alag-alag button components dikhna) ki problem ko solve karta hai.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapka Assets Panel (library) 'khichdi' ban jayega. Aapko (aur aapki team ko) sahi component dhoondhne mein bohot time lagega. (e.g., "Secondary Disabled button kaun sa hai?"). Aap 'Interactive Components' (Module 8) nahi bana payenge, jo prototype ko 'real' (asli) feel dete hain (jaise button par hover karna).
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Component Set:** Jab aap variants banate hain, Figma un sabko ek 'purple dotted line' waale container mein daal deta hai. Is poore group ko 'Component Set' kehte hain.
    * **Properties (Gun):** Yeh 'categories' (shreniyaan) hain jinhe aap define karte hain. (e.g., Property 1: `State`, Property 2: `Type`).
    * **Values (Maan):** Yeh har property ke 'options' (vikalp) hain. (e.g., `State` ki values: `Default`, `Hover`. `Type` ki values: `Primary`, `Secondary`).
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Hamare 'Primary Button' (Topic 6.1) ke do 'State' variants banana: `Default` aur `Hover`.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Apne 'ğŸ§© Components' page par jaayein.
        2.  Aapka 'Primary Button' â– (Master Component) wahan hai. Use select karein.
        3.  Right Panel mein (jahan component ka naam hai), `+` (Add Variant) icon par click karein.
        4.  **ğŸš€ Quick run (Output 1):** Figma ek 'Component Set' (purple dotted line) bana dega aur uske andar aapke button ki ek copy (variant) bana dega.
        5.  Ab 'Component Set' (poora purple box) ko select karein. Right Panel (Component section) mein dekhein. Wahan "Property 1: Default" likha hoga.
        6.  "Property 1" ka naam badal kar `State` rakhein.
        7.  Ab pehle button (original waala) ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'State' property ki value `Default` likhi hogi. Use `Default` hi rehne dein.
        8.  Doosre button (naya waala) ko select karein. Uski 'State' value ko `Variant 2` se badal kar `Hover` rakhein.
        9.  **Edit the Hover state:** Is doosre (Hover) button ko select karke uska 'Fill' (color) thoda dark kar dein (Style detach karke).
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run (Final Output):** Aapke paas *ek* 'Primary Button' component set hai. Ab 'Assets' panel se ise design mein drag karein. Right Panel mein aapko ek 'State' naam ka dropdown (ya toggle) dikhega, jisse aap use `Default` aur `Hover` ke beech switch kar sakte hain.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * **Bahut saare properties bana dena.** (Koshish karein 3 properties (e.g., State, Type, Size) se zyada na hon, warna complex ho jaata hai).
    * **Naam galat dena.** ( agar aapne naam `State=Default` aur `State=Hover` rakha, toh Figma use 'State' property mein daal dega. Agar aapne `Default` aur `Hover` rakha, toh 2 alag-alag component ban jayenge). Naming hi sab kuch hai.
    * Alag-alag size (e.g., ek button 48px, doosra 50px) ke variants ko combine karna. (Variants hamesha same size se shuru hone chahiye).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main 2 alag-alag component (Button-Default â–, Button-Hover â–) kyun nahi bana sakta? Yeh (Variants) toh confusing hai."
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Shuruaat mein 2 component aasan lagte hain. Par jab aapke paas 2 Types (Primary, Secondary) * 3 States (Default, Hover, Disabled) * 2 Sizes (Small, Large) honge... toh aapko 2 x 3 x 2 = **12 alag-alag component** Assets panel mein manage karne padenge. Variants ke saath, aapke paas *sirf 1 component* ('Button') hoga, jismein 3 dropdown honge (Type, State, Size).
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Design System mein *har* component variants ka use karke banta hai. Isse library (Assets panel) super clean rehti hai. Designer bas 'Button' drag karta hai aur Right Panel se use configure (set) karta hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Ek 'Checkbox' component. Iske variants honge: `State=Unchecked`, `State=Checked`. `State=Disabled-Unchecked`, `State=Disabled-Checked`. Yeh sab *ek hi* component set ('Checkbox' â–) ke andar honge.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Component select karein -> Right Panel mein `+` (Variants) par click karein.
    * Poore 'Component Set' (purple box) ko select karke 'Properties' (e.g., `State`, `Type`, `Size`) define karein.
    * Har variant ko select karke uski property 'Value' (e.g., `Default`, `Primary`, `Small`) set karein.
    * Naming (e.g., `Button/Primary/Hover`) se bhi Figma automatic variants bana deta hai.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Properties aur Values kya hain?** Property = Category (e.g., `Size`). Value = Option (e.g., `Small`, `Large`).
    * **Main ek component set mein naya variant kaise add karun?** Set ke andar kisi bhi variant ko select karein aur uske paas `+` icon dabayein (ya copy-paste karein).
    * **Mera variant switch (toggle) ki jagah dropdown kyun dikha raha hai?** Agar property ki values `True`/`False`, `Yes`/`No`, ya `On`/`Off` hon, toh Figma *automatic* ek 'toggle switch' (switch) bana deta hai. (Yeh 6.3 mein dekhenge).
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Button' waali exercise (Task) ko poora karein.
    * 2. Ek naya 'Property' (Type) add karein. Ab aapke paas 4 variant hone chahiye: (State=Default, Type=Primary), (State=Hover, Type=Primary), (State=Default, Type=Secondary), (State=Hover, Type=Secondary). (Secondary waale ka color badal dein).
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Interactive Components (Module 8):** Variants ka asli jaadu jab hum unhe prototype karenge.

---

### 6.3: Advanced Component Properties (Boolean, Instance Swap, Text)

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Advanced Component Properties (Component ko super-smart banana).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Yeh 3 'advanced properties' hain jo aap apne *Master* component par set karte hain, taaki 'Instance' (copy) ko edit karna bohot aasan ho jaaye. Yeh 'Variants' ke saath (ya unke bina) kaam karte hain.
    * **Text Property:** Aap 'Instance' ko select karke, *Right Panel* se hi text (e.g., "Button Text") badal sakte hain (bina text par double-click kiye).
    * **Boolean Property:** Yeh 'Instance' par ek `On/Off` switch (toggle) banata hai. Isse aap component ke andar ki koi layer (e.g., ek 'Icon') ko *dikha* (show) ya *chhupa* (hide) sakte hain. (Naam: `Show Icon? True/False`).
    * **Instance Swap Property:** Yeh 'Instance' par ek 'dropdown' banata hai, jisse aap us component ke *andar* ke ek 'nested instance' (e.g., ek icon) ko kisi doosre component (e.g., alag icon) se *badal* (swap) sakte hain.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh aapke components ko "asli" (real) product jaisa bana deta hai. Designer (jo aapki component library use kar raha hai) ko 'Instance' ke andar jaakar (double-click karke) layers ko dhoondhna aur edit nahi karna padta. Saare common badlaav (text, icon, show/hide) *seedha Right Panel* se ho jaate hain.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):**
    * **Text:** Har component jismein text hai (Button, List Item, Card Title).
    * **Boolean:** Jab component mein koi 'optional' (vaikalpik) element ho (e.g., ek button mein *optional* 'Left Icon', ya ek card mein *optional* 'Tag').
    * **Instance Swap:** Jab component mein ek 'placeholder' (jagah) ho jahan user alag-alag cheezein daal sake (e.g., ek 'Button' jismein user `Icon-Home` ya `Icon-Settings` select kar sake).
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aapke components 'dumb' (bekaar) honge. Agar kisi ko button ka text badalna hai, toh use Instance (â™¢) par 4 baar double-click karke text layer tak pahunchna padega. Agar icon hatana hai, toh use layer ko manually hide (aankh ğŸ‘ï¸ band) karna padega (jo ek 'override' hai aur reset ho sakta hai).
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * Yeh saari properties 'Master Component' (â–) ke *andar* waali layer par apply ki jaati hain.
    * **Master Component (â–) ko select karein.**
    * Right Panel mein 'Properties' section mein `+` icon par click karein -> `Text`, `Boolean`, ya `Instance Swap` chunein.
    * Phir us property ko *andar* waali layer se 'link' (jodein) karein.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Hamare 'Primary Button' â– ko 3 properties dena: Text, Boolean (Show Icon), aur Instance Swap (Icon).
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Apne 'ğŸ§© Components' page par 'Primary Button' â– (Master) par jaayein.
        2.  Button (Auto Layout) ke andar ek 'Icon' (e.g., ek Star â­ï¸ instance) add karein (text ke left mein).
        3.  **Text Property:** Button ke andar waali 'Text Layer' ("Button Text") ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'Text' section mein, 'Content' ke paas `Apply text property` (diamond jaisa) icon par click karein. `Create new property` chunein, naam dein "Label" aur 'Create' karein.
        4.  **Boolean Property:** Button ke andar waali 'Icon' (Star â­ï¸) layer ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'Layer' section (jahan ğŸ‘ï¸ icon hai) ke paas `Apply boolean property` (diamond jaisa) icon par click karein. `Create new property` chunein, naam dein "Show Icon" aur Value `True` (default mein dikhega) rakhein. 'Create' karein.
        5.  **Instance Swap Property:** Wahi 'Icon' (Star â­ï¸) layer select rakhein. Right Panel mein *component ke naam* (e.g., "Star") ke paas `Apply instance swap property` (diamond jaisa) icon par click karein. `Create new property` chunein, naam dein "Icon" aur 'Create' karein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Ab apni 'Design' page par is button ki 'Instance' (â™¢) ko select karein. Right Panel dekhein! Aapko 3 naye controls milenge:
        * Ek text field "Label" (jahan se aap text badal sakte hain).
        * Ek toggle switch "Show Icon" (jisse aap icon hide/show kar sakte hain).
        * Ek dropdown "Icon" (jisse aap 'Star' ko kisi aur icon component se badal sakte hain).
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * In properties ke baare mein pata hi na hona.
    * 'Instance' par properties dhoondhna. (Yaad rakhein: Properties hamesha 'Master' â– par *set* ki jaati hain, aur 'Instance' â™¢ par *use* ki jaati hain).
    * Boolean (Show/Hide) aur Variant (2 alag component) mein confuse hona. (Agar 'Icon' aur 'No Icon' waale button *dikne* mein bohot alag hain (e.g., padding alag hai), toh 'Variant' (Topic 6.2) behtar hai. Agar sirf icon hide karna hai, toh 'Boolean' (Topic 6.3) behtar hai).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Yeh bohot complicated hai. Main bas 'Instance' par double-click karke text badal loonga."
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Aap kar sakte hain. Par jab aapka component 'nested' (gehra) hoga (e.g., Card -> Header -> User Info -> Text Layer), toh text badalne ke liye 4 baar double-click karna padega. 'Text Property' se yeh 1 click (Right Panel) mein ho jaata hai.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** **Yeh properties hi professional Design System ka 'API' (controls) hoti hain.** Designer (jo library use kar raha hai) ko *kabhi bhi* component ke andar jaana hi nahi padta. Saara kaam Right Panel (jo 'Properties Panel' ban jaata hai) se hota hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Ek 'List Item' component. Ismein `Text Property` ("List Title"), `Boolean Property` ("Show Chevron >"), aur `Instance Swap Property` ("Left Icon") hota hai. Designer 10 second mein 5 alag-alag list items bana sakta hai, sab Right Panel se.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Har text layer ko `Text Property` se link karo.
    * Har *optional* (vaikalpik) layer (jaise icon, badge) ko `Boolean Property` se link karo.
    * Har *swappable* (badalne laayak) nested component (jaise icon) ko `Instance Swap Property` se link karo.
    * Properties hamesha 'Master' â– par hi set hoti hain.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **In properties ko edit/delete kaise karein?** 'Master Component' (â–) ko select karein. Right Panel mein 'Properties' section mein list dikhegi. Wahan se edit/delete karein.
    * **Text Property vs Instance par text override karna?** Dono kaam karte hain. 'Text Property' bas zyada 'official' (saaf) tareeka hai aur Right Panel mein control deta hai.
    * **Boolean Property vs Variant (e.g., State=Icon, State=No Icon)?** Boolean tez hai, par agar icon hatne se Auto Layout ki padding/spacing bhi badalni chahiye, toh 'Variant' behtar control deta hai.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Button' waali exercise (Task) ko poora karein.
    * 2. Ek 'User Profile' component banayein (Avatar + Name). 'Name' ko `Text Property` dein aur 'Avatar' (jo ek component instance hona chahiye) ko `Instance Swap Property` dein.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * (Yeh Figma ka advanced core feature hai. Practice hi key hai).

---

### 6.4: Using the Assets Panel

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Using the Assets Panel ğŸ—ƒï¸ (Apne components ko dhoondhna aur use karna).
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** 'Assets' panel **Left Panel** (Layers ke baad waala tab) hai. Yeh aapki file (aur aapki team library) ke *saare* components (â–) ki 'library' (pustakaalay) hai. Yahan se aap components ko 'drag-and-drop' karke apne design (Frames) mein 'Instances' (â™¢) ki tarah use karte hain.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yahi woh jagah hai jahan 'Components' ka (reuse) fayda milta hai. Agar aapne component bana diya par use 'Assets' panel se drag nahi kiya (balki Master ko hi copy-paste kiya), toh component ka poora matlab hi khatam ho jaata hai.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab aapne 'Master Component' (â–) bana liya ho (apne 'Components' page par), aur ab aap use apne *asli* design (e.g., 'Home Page' frame) mein istemaal karna chahte hon. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh "Mera master component kahan save hua hai?" aur "Main component ki copy (Instance) kaise banaun?" ki problem ko solve karta hai.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** Aap components ka fayda nahi utha payenge. Aap Master component ko hi copy-paste karte rahenge, jo bohot bura workflow hai (aap galti se master ko edit kar denge). Aapki file messy (gandi) ho jayegi.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Location:** Left Panel (Layers ke paas waala tab).
    * **Search Bar:** Sabse zaroori. Agar aapke paas 500 component hain, toh aap yahan 'Button' search kar sakte hain.
    * **Organization:** Components us 'Page' ke naam ke neeche dikhte hain jispar woh banaye gaye the (e.g., "ğŸ§© Components" page).
    * **Folders:** Agar aapne component ka naam slash `/` se rakha tha (e.g., `Button/Primary`), toh Assets panel mein `Button` naam ka ek 'folder' ban jayega, jiske andar `Primary` component hoga.
    * **Drag-and-Drop:** Yahan se component ko kheench kar (drag) canvas par laane se *hamesha* ek 'Instance' (â™¢) banti hai.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Hamare 'Primary Button' component (jo 'ğŸ§© Components' page par hai) ko 'Home Page' Frame mein use karna.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  Apne 'ğŸ“± High-Fidelity' (ya 'Home Page') page par jaayein.
        2.  `F` daba kar ek 'iPhone' frame banayein.
        3.  Ab **Left Panel** mein 'Layers' tab se 'Assets' tab par click karein.
        4.  Aapko "Local components" ke neeche "ğŸ§© Components" (aapke page ka naam) dikhega.
        5.  Uske andar, aapka 'Primary Button' component dikhega.
        6.  Use wahan se *drag* (kheench kar) apne 'iPhone' frame ke *andar* *drop* (chhod) dein.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapke iPhone frame mein ek 'Instance' (â™¢) aa gayi hai. Ab aap isse copy-paste (Alt-drag) karke 10 aur button bana sakte hain, woh sab 'Instance' hi rahenge.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * 'Assets' panel ka istemaal hi na karna.
    * 'Master Component' (â–) ko 'Components' page se *copy* (Ctrl+C) karke design page par *paste* (Ctrl+V) karna. (Yeh bhi Instance hi banata hai, par 'Assets' panel se drag karna behtar workflow hai).
    * Components ka naam theek se (slash `/` ke saath) na dena, jisse Assets panel mein 100 components ki *ek* lambi list ban jaati hai (bina folders ke).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Assets panel mein 'Local components' aur 'Team Library' (e.g., 'Google Material') mein kya fark hai?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** 'Local components' woh hain jo aapne *issi file* mein banaye hain. 'Team Library' (Module 7) woh components hain jo kisi *aur* file mein banaye gaye the aur aap unhe yahan 'import' karke use kar rahe hain.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Designer 90% time 'Team Library' waale components (jo Design System team ne banaye hain) ko 'Assets' panel se drag karke hi apna design banata hai. Woh naye 'local' component bohot kam banata hai.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Aapko 10 'Product Cards' ka grid banana hai. Aap 'Assets' panel mein jaate hain -> 'Card' folder -> 'Product Card' ko drag karke grid mein daalte hain -> Phir use Alt-drag karke 9 baar aur copy karte hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * Components (Instances) laane ke liye hamesha 'Assets' panel ka use karein.
    * Apne components ko hamesha slash `/` waali naming se organize karein (e.g., `Icon/24px/Home`, `Button/Primary/Default`).
    * Search bar ka bharpoor istemaal karein.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Mera component 'Assets' panel mein nahi dikh raha!** Check karein ki (1) aapne use component (â–) banaya hai (Ctrl+Alt+K), aur (2) aap 'Assets' tab mein hain, 'Layers' tab mein nahi.
    * **'Assets' panel mein component ka preview (thumbnail) ajeeb dikh raha hai.** Figma 'Master Component' (â–) ke Frame ka preview dikhata hai. Apne 'Components' page par Master component ke frame ko clean rakhein.
12. **ğŸ‹ï¸â€â™€ï¸ Practice exercise (Lab):**
    * 1. 'Assets panel' se 'Button' drag karne waali exercise (Task) ko poora karein.
    * 2. 5 alag-alag icons (e.g., Home, Search, Profile) ko component (â–) banayein. Unka naam `Icon/Home`, `Icon/Search`, `Icon/Profile` rakhein. Ab 'Assets' panel mein dekhein, 'Icon' naam ka folder ban gaya hoga.
13. **ğŸ“š Further reading / related tools / plugins:**
    * **Team Library (Module 7):** Assets panel ki agli superpower.

---

Yeh tha hamara Module 6! ğŸš€ Aapne Figma ka sabse bada powerhouse featureâ€”Components, Variants, aur Propertiesâ€”seekh liya hai. Aapne 'Styles' (Atoms) aur 'Components' (Molecules) ko jodna seekh liya hai.

Aap 'Design System' banane ke bohot kareeb aa gaye hain.

Jab aap ready hon, bas **"Module 7 shuru karo"** likh dena, aur hum seekhenge ki in components ko poori team ke saath 'publish' (share) kaise karte hain aur 'Variables' (Styles ka naya version) kya hote hain!


=============================================================

Chalo bhai, shuru karte hain aapke Figma (Beginner-to-Job-Ready) notes ka Module 7!

Module 5 aur 6 mein humne 'Design System' ke building blocksâ€”Styles (Atoms) aur Components (Molecules)â€”banana seekha. Ab Module 7 mein, hum seekhenge ki in sabko jodkar ek poora 'Design System' kaise manage kiya jaata hai, team ke saath share (publish) kaise kiya jaata hai, aur 'Variables' jaisi advanced cheezon ka istemaal kaise kiya jaata hai.

---

### 7.1: Design Systems (Concept)

1.  **ğŸ¯ Title / Short Summary:** Design Systems (Concept) ğŸ—ƒï¸ (Design ka 'Single Source of Truth').
2.  **ğŸ¤” Kya hai? (What?):** Design System (DS) aapke product ko banane ke liye zaroori har cheez ka ek **central (kendriye) collection** hai. Ismein aapke reusable **Components** (Button, Card), **Styles** (Colors, Fonts), **Guidelines** (niyam, jaise 8-point grid), aur **Documentation** (kaise use karein) sab ek jagah hote hain.
3.  **ğŸ’¡ Kyu important hai? (Why?):** Yeh do cheezein deta hai: **Consistency (ek-jaisa-pan)** aur **Speed/Efficiency (tezi)**. Jab poori company (100 designers aur 500 developers) *ek hi* Design System ka *ek hi* 'Button' component use karti hai, toh poora product (website, iOS app, Android app) ek jaisa dikhta hai aur tezi se banta hai.
4.  **â° Kab/Kahan use karein? (When/Where?):** Jab bhi aapka product 'scale' (bada) ho raha ho. Jab aapki team mein 1 se zyada designer ho. Jab aapka product 1 se zyada platform (e.g., Web aur Mobile) par ho. Yeh *kis* problem ko solve karta hai? Yeh "khichdi" design ki problem ko solve karta hai, jahan har designer apna alag 'blue' color aur apna alag 'button' design bana deta hai, jisse product inconsistent (alag-alag) dikhta hai.
5.  **âŒ Agar use nahi kiya to kya hoga? (If not used / consequences):** **Inconsistency:** Aapki app mein 5 alag-alag tarah ke buttons honge. **Slow Workflow:** Har designer har baar zero se button banayega. **Maintenance Nightmare:** Jab brand ka color badlega, toh developers ko 100 alag-alag jagah CSS code change karna padega. Design System ke bina, bade products (jaise Google, Airbnb) banana impossible hai.
6.  **ğŸ§‘â€ğŸ« Step-by-step explanation / Concept breakdown:**
    * **Foundation (Atoms):** Colors, Typography (Fonts), Spacing (8-pt grid), Grids. (Yeh humne Module 5 mein kiya).
    * **Components (Molecules/Organisms):** Reusable UI elements (Buttons, Inputs, Cards). (Yeh humne Module 6 mein kiya).
    * **Guidelines & Documentation:** Sabse zaroori. Yeh 'niyam' (rules) hote hain. Jaise: "Primary button kab use karein" (Do's) aur "Secondary button kab *nahi* use karein" (Don'ts). Yeh aksar ek alag website (jaise 'Zeroheight' ya 'Storybook') par hote hain.
7.  **ğŸ’» UI Example(s) / Step-by-Step Guide:**
    * **Task:** Ek Design System ka structure sochna.
    * **âœï¸ Option-by-option explanation:**
        1.  **Figma File (UI Kit):** Yeh aapki 'Library' file hoti hai (jise hum 7.3 mein publish karenge). Ismein aapke saare 'Pages' (Module 1.2) organized hote hain:
            * `Cover:` Thumbnail.
            * `Styles & Atoms:` Colors, Typography, Shadows.
            * `ğŸ§© Components:` Saare Master Components (Buttons, Inputs, etc.).
            * `Guidelines:` Spacing, Grids, Do's/Don'ts ke examples.
        2.  **Documentation (Website):** Ek alag website jo developers ko batati hai ki 'Button' component ka code (e.g., React code) kya hai.
    * **ğŸš€ Quick run expected output:** Aapke paas ek central Figma file hai (UI Kit) jo aapke product ka 'single source of truth' hai.
8.  **ğŸ Common beginner mistakes:**
    * Sochna ki 'Design System' sirf ek 'Figma Component Library' hai. (Galat! Yeh library + *documentation aur guidelines* (niyam) hai).
    * 'Guidelines' (niyam) waala hissa chhod dena. (Bina niyam ke, log component ko galat tareeke se use karenge).
    * Har cheez ko system mein daal dena. (Sirf *reusable* cheezein hi DS ka hissa hoti hain).
9.  **ğŸŒ Real-World Workflow Scenario (The "How-To-Use"):**
    * **â“ Beginner's Core Question:** "Main ek akela freelancer/student hoon. Kya mujhe itne bade 'Design System' ki zaroorat hai?"
    * **ğŸ•µï¸â€â™‚ï¸ Solo Freelancer/Student Workflow:** Aapko poore 'Design System' (documentation website ke saath) ki zaroorat nahi hai. Lekin aapko ek **'UI Kit'** ki 100% zaroorat hai. 'UI Kit' aapka apna personal Design System hai. Yani, aapki ek Figma file jismein aapke saare reusable Colors, Text Styles, aur Components (Button, Input, Card) rakhe hain, taaki aap apna *khud ka* project tezi se (fast) bana sakein.
    * **ğŸ‘©â€ğŸ’» Professional Design Team Workflow:** Badi companies (jaise Google, Microsoft, Atlassian) mein ek *dedicated 'Design System Team'* (5-10 log) hoti hai. Unka kaam sirf Design System (components, documentation) ko banana aur maintain karna hota hai. Baaki 100 'Product Designers' (jo features bana rahe hain) us DS ko sirf 'consume' (use) karte hain.
    * **ğŸ’° Real-World Example:** Google ka **'Material Design'**, Apple ka **'Human Interface Guidelines (HIG)'**, aur Atlassian ka **'Atlassian Design System'**... yeh sab duniya ke best Design Systems hain.
10. **âœ… Quick checklist / Best Practices:**
    * **Reusable:** Har cheez reusable honi chahiye.
    * **Consistent:** Sab kuch ek jaisa dikhna aur behave karna chahiye.
    * **Documented:** Har cheez ke niyam (rules) likhe hone chahiye.
    * **Single Source of Truth (SSOT):** Sab kuch *ek* central jagah par hona chahiye.
11. **â“ Key Designer Questions (FAQs):**
    * **Design System vs Style Guide vs UI Kit?**
